Structure\n39\t\n40\tSuperMac uses an organized, hierarchical command structure:\n41\t\n42\t```bash\n43\tmac <category> <action> [arguments]\n44\t```\n45\t\n46\t### 📋 Available Categories\n47\t\n48\t| Category | Icon | Description | Example Commands |\n49\t|----------|------|-------------|------------------|\n50\t| **finder** | 📁 | File visibility and Finder management | `restart`, `toggle-hidden`, `reveal` |\n51\t| **wifi** | 🌐 | WiFi control and management | `on`, `off`, `toggle`, `status` |\n52\t| **network** | 📡 | Network information and troubleshooting | `ip`, `public-ip`, `flush-dns` |\n53\t| **system** | 🖥️ | System information and maintenance | `info`, `cleanup`, `battery` |\n54\t| **dev** | 💻 | Developer tools and utilities | `kill-port`, `servers`, `localhost` |\n55\t| **display** | 🖥️ | Display and appearance settings | `brightness`, `dark-mode`, `night-shift` |\n56\t| **dock** | 🚢 | Dock management and positioning | `position`, `autohide`, `size` |\n57\t| **audio** | 🔊 | Audio control and device management | `volume`, `mute`, `devices` |\n58\t\n59\t## 🎨 Beautiful Help System\n60\t\n61\tSuperMac features a stunning help system with visual hierarchy:\n62\t\n63\t```bash\n64\t╭─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╮\n65\t│                  🚀 SuperMac v2.1.0                    │\n66\t│                Built by CosmoLabs                       │\n67\t╰─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────╯\n68\t\n69\t┌─ 📁 FINDER ──────────────────────────────────────────────┐\n70\t│  restart               Restart Finder application       │\n71\t│  toggle-hidden         Toggle hidden file visibility    │\n72\t│  show-hidden           Show system files               │\n73\t│  hide-hidden           Hide system files               │\n74\t│  reveal <path>         Reveal file/folder in Finder    │\n75\t└──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘\n76\t```\n77\t\n78\t## ⚡ Quick Commands\n79\t\n80\t### Global Shortcuts\n81\t```bash\n82\tmac ip                    # Quick IP lookup\n83\tmac cleanup               # System cleanup\n84\tmac dark                  # Switch to dark mode\n85\tmac light                 # Switch to light mode\n86\tmac kp 3000               # Kill process on port 3000\n87\t```\n88\t\n89\t### Essential Commands\n90\t```bash\n91\t# Finder Management\n92\tmac finder restart                # Fix unresponsive Finder\n93\tmac finder toggle-hidden          # Show/hide system files\n94\tmac finder reveal ~/.ssh          # Open .ssh folder in Finder\n95\t\n96\t# Display Control\n97\tmac display brightness 75         # Set brightness to 75%\n98\tmac display dark-mode             # Switch to dark mode\n99\tmac display night-shift on        # Enable Night Shift\n100\t\n101\t# Development\n102\tmac dev kill-port 3000            # Kill process on port\n103\tmac dev servers                   # List running servers\n104\tmac dev localhost 8080            # Open localhost in browser\n105\t\n106\t# Network\n107\tmac network ip                    # Show local IP\n108\tmac network public-ip             # Show public IP\n109\tmac network flush-dns             # Clear DNS cache\n110\t\n111\t# System Maintenance\n112\tmac system info                   # System information\n113\tmac system cleanup                # Deep cleanup\n114\tmac system battery                # Battery status\n115\t```\n116\t\n117\t## 🔍 Discovery Features\n118\t\n119\t### Smart Help System\n120\t```bash\n121\tmac help                          # Show all 🛠️ SuperMac Development Guide\n2\t\n3\t## 📋 Overview\n4\t\n5\tSuperMac is a modular, professional command-line tool for macOS built with a clean architecture that makes it easy to add new commands and maintain existing functionality.\n6\t\n7\t## 🏗️ Architecture\n8\t\n9\t### File Structure\n10\t```\n11\tSuperMac/\n12\t├── bin/\n13\t│   ├── mac                 # Main dispatcher (entry point)\n14\t│   └── install.sh          # Installation script\n15\t├── lib/                    # Modular command libraries\n16\t│   ├── utils.sh           # Shared utilities & formatting\n17\t│   ├── finder.sh          # Finder commands\n18\t│   ├── display.sh         # Display commands\n19\t│   ├── network.sh         # Network commands\n20\t│   ├── system.sh          # System commands\n21\t│   ├── dev.sh             # Developer commands\n22\t│   ├── dock.sh            # Dock management\n23\t│   └── audio.sh           # Audio control\n24\t├── config/\n25\t│   └── config.json        # User configuration\n26\t├── docs/\n27\t│   ├── README.md          # Main documentation\n28\t│   └── DEVELOPMENT.md     # This file\n29\t└── tests/\n30\t    └── test.sh            # Test suite\n31\t```\n32\t\n33\t### Design Principles\n34\t\n35\t1. **Modular**: Each category is a separate module\n36\t2. **Consistent**: All modules follow the same patterns\n37\t3. **Discoverable**: Beautiful help system with search\n38\t4. **Safe**: Input validation and confirmation for destructive operations\n39\t5. **Fast**: Minimal overhead, optimized for quick execution\n40\t6. **Professional**: Enterprise-ready with proper error handling\n41\t\n42\t## 🧩 Module Architecture\n43\t\n44\t### Module Template\n45\t\n46\tEvery module follows this structure:\n47\t\n48\t```bash\n49\t#!/bin/bash\n50\t\n51\t# =============================================================================\n52\t# SuperMac - [ModuleName] Module\n53\t# =============================================================================\n54\t# Brief description of module functionality\n55\t# \n56\t# Commands:\n57\t#   command1 - Description\n58\t#   command2 - Description\n59\t#\n60\t# Built by CosmoLabs - https://cosmolabs.org\n61\t# =============================================================================\n62\t\n63\t# =============================================================================\n64\t# Module Functions\n65\t# =============================================================================\n66\t\n67\tmodulename_function1() {\n68\t    # Implementation\n69\t}\n70\t\n71\tmodulename_function2() {\n72\t    # Implementation\n73\t}\n74\t\n75\t# =============================================================================\n76\t# Module Help System\n77\t# =============================================================================\n78\t\n79\tmodulename_help() {\n80\t    print_category_header \"modulename\" \"🔥\" 70\n81\t    \n82\t    printf \"${PURPLE}│${NC}  %-20s %-40s ${PURPLE}│${NC}\\n\" \"command1\" \"Description\"\n83\t    printf \"${PURPLE}│${NC}  %-20s %-40s ${PURPLE}│${NC}\\n\" \"command2\" \"Description\"\n84\t    \n85\t    print_category_footer 70\n86\t    echo \"\"\n87\t    \n88\t    print_header \"Examples:\"\n89\t    echo \"  mac modulename command1             # Example usage\"\n90\t    echo \"\"\n91\t}\n92\t\n93\t# Search function for this module\n94\tmodulename_search() {\n95\t    local search_term=\"$1\"\n96\t    local results=\"\"\n97\t    \n98\t    if [[ \"keyword\" == *\"$search_term\"* ]]; then\n99\t        results+=\"  mac modulename command1          Description\\n\"\n100\t    fi\n101\t    \n102\t    if [[ -n \"$results\" ]]; then\n103\t        echo -e \"$results\"\n104\t    fi\n105\t}\n106\t\n107\t# =============================================================================\n108\t# Module Dispatcher\n109\t# =============================================================================\n110\t\n111\tmodulename_dispatch() {\n112\t    local action=\"$1\"\n113\t    shift  # Remove action from arguments\n114\t    \n115\t    case \"$action\" in\n116\t        \"command1\")\n117\t            modulename_function1 \"$@\"\n118\t            ;;\n119\t        \"command2\")\n120\t            modulename_function2 \"$@\"\n121\t            ;;\n122\t        \"help\"|\"-h\"|\"--help\")\n123\t            modulename_help\n124\t            ;;\n125\t        *)\n126\t            print_error \"Unknown modulename action: $action\"\n127\t            echo \"\"\n128\t            print_info \"Available actions: command1, command2\"\n129\t            print_info \"Use 'mac help modulename' for detailed information\"\n130\t            return 1\n131\t            ;;\n132\t    esac\n133\t}\n134\t\n135\tprint_debug \"ModuleName module loaded successfully\"\n136\t```\n137\t\n138\t### Required Functions\n139\t\n140\tEvery module MUST implement these functions:\n141\t\n142\t1. **`modulename_dispatch()`** - Routes actions to appropriate functions\n143\t2. **`modulename_help()`** - Provides detailed help for the module\n144\t3. **`modulename_search()`** - Enables search functionality\n145\t\n146\t### Optional Functions\n147\t\n148\tModules can implement these for enhanced functionality:\n149\t\n150\t- **`modulename_status()`** - Show current status/settings\n151\t- **`modulename_reset()`** - Reset module settings to defaults\n152\t- **`modulename_validate()`** - Validate module requirements\n153\t\n154\t## 🎨 Styling Guidelines\n155\t\n156\t### Output Functions\n157\t\n158\tUse the standard output functions from `utils.sh`:\n159\t\n160\t```bash\n161\tprint_success \"Operation completed!\"       # Green checkmark\n162\tprint_error \"Something went wrong\"         # Red X\n163\tprint_info \"Information message\"           # Blue info icon\n164\tprint_warning \"Proceed with caution\"       # Yellow warning\n165\tprint_header \"Section Header\"              # Bold blue text\n166\tprint_debug \"Debug information\"            # Gray text (only in debug mode)\n167\t```\n168\t\n169\t### Visual Formatting\n170\t\n171\tUse the box drawing functions for beautiful output:\n172\t\n173\t```bash\n174\tprint_category_header \"category\" \"🔥\" 70   # Category header with emoji\n175\tprint_category_footer 70                  # Matching footer\n176\tprint_banner \"SuperMac v2.1.0\"           # Centered banner\n177\tprint_box \"Important message\"             # Simple box around text\n178\t```\n179\t\n180\t### Color Usage\n181\t\n182\tColors are available as constants:\n183\t- `$RED`, `$GREEN`, `$YELLOW`, `$BLUE`, `$PURPLE`, `$CYAN`\n184\t- `$BOLD`, `$DIM`, `$UNDERLINE`\n185\t- `$NC` (No Color) - always end colored text with this\n186\t\n187\t## 🔧 Adding a New Module\n188\t\n189\t### Step 1: Create Module File\n190\t\n191\tCreate `lib/newmodule.sh` following the module template above.\n192\t\n193\t### Step 2: Update Main Dispatcher\n194\t\n195\tAdd your module to `bin/mac`:\n196\t\n197\t```bash\n198\t# In the CATEGORIES array\n199\tdeclare -A CATEGORIES=(\n200\t    # ... existing categories ...\n201\t    [\"newmodule\"]=\"🔥:Description of new module\"\n202\t)\n203\t\n204\t# In the route_command function, the module will be automatically loaded\n205\t```\n206\t\n207\t### Step 3: Update Configuration\n208\t\n209\tAdd your module to `config/config.json`:\n210\t\n211\t```json\n212\t{\n213\t  \"categories\": {\n214\t    \"newmodule\": {\n215\t      \"enabled\": true,\n216\t      \"description\": \"Description of new module\"\n217\t    }\n218\t  }\n219\t}\n220\t```\n221\t\n222\t### Step 4: Add Tests\n223\t\n224\tAdd tests for your module in `tests/test.sh`:\n225\t\n226\t```bash\n227\ttest_newmodule() {\n228\t    test_header \"Testing New Module\"\n229\t    \n230\t    count_test\n231\t    if \"$BIN_DIR/mac\" newmodule help >/dev/null 2>&1; then\n232\t        test_success \"New module help works\"\n233\t    else\n234\t        test_fail \"New module help failed\"\n235\t    fi\n236\t}\n237\t```\n238\t\n239\t### Step 5: Update Documentation\n240\t\n241\tAdd your module to the main README.md and any relevant documentation.\n242\t\n243\t## 🧪 Testing\n244\t\n245\t### Running Tests\n246\t\n247\t```bash\n248\t# Run all tests\n249\tbash tests/test.sh\n250\t\n251\t# Test specific module\n252\tbash tests/test.sh newmodule\n253\t\n254\t# Test with debug output\n255\tbash tests/test.sh --debug\n256\t```\n257\t\n258\t### Test Types\n259\t\n260\t1. **Syntax Tests** - Verify bash syntax is valid\n261\t2. **Module Loading** - Ensure modules can be sourced\n262\t3. **Function Existence** - Check required functions exist\n263\t4. **Functional Tests** - Test actual command execution\n264\t5. **Performance Tests** - Verify startup time and speed\n265\t\n266\t### Writing Good Tests\n267\t\n268\t```bash\n269\ttest_new_feature() {\n270\t    test_header \"Feature Tests\"\n271\t    \n272\t    # Test success case\n273\t    count_test\n274\t    if expected_command_succeeds; then\n275\t        test_success \"Feature works correctly\"\n276\t    else\n277\t        test_fail \"Feature failed\"\n278\t    fi\n279\t    \n280\t    # Test error case\n281\t    count_test\n282\t    if ! expected_command_fails; then\n283\t        test_success \"Error handling works\"\n284\t    else\n285\t        test_fail \"Error handling broken\"\n286\t    fi\n287\t}\n288\t```\n289\t\n290\t## 📝 Code Standards\n291\t\n292\t### Naming Conventions\n293\t\n294\t- **Functions**: `modulename_functionname()` (underscore separated)\n295\t- **Variables**: ;;\n69\t    esac\n70\t}\n71\t\n72\tfinder_show_hidden() {\n73\t    local current_state\n74\t    current_state=$(finder_get_hidden_state)\n75\t    \n76\t    if [[ \"$current_state\" == \"visible\" ]]; \n198\t    printf \"\\r${BLUE}[\"\n199\t    printf \"%*s\" \"$filled\" \"\" | tr ' ' \"$fill_char\"\n200\t    printf \"%*s\" \"$empty\" \"\" | tr ' ' \"$empty_char\"\n201\t    printf \"] %d%% \n294\t    echo -e \"${YELLOW}$prompt${NC} \"\n295\t    read -r response\n296\t    \n297\t    case \"$response\" in\n298\t        [yY]|[yY][eE][sS])\n299\t            return 0\n300\t     *)\n308\t            print_warning \"Please answer yes or no.\"\n309\t            confirm \"$1\" \"$default\"\n310\t            ;;\n311\t    esac\n312\t}\n313\t\n314\t# Prompt for input with      - Show WiFi connection status\n13\t#   scan           - Scan for available networks\n14\t#   connect <name> - Connect to network\n15\t#   forget <name>  - Forget saved network\n16\t#   info \n90\t    if [[ -z \"$interface\" ]]; then\n91\t        print_error \"WiFi interface not found\"\n92\t        return 1\n93\t    fi\n94\t    \n95\t    local current_state\n96\t \n122\t    print_info \"Current WiFi state: $current_state\"\n123\t    \n124\t    case \"$current_state\" in\n125\t        \"On\")\n126\t            wifi_off\n127\t            ;;\n128\t \n466\t    case \"$action\" in\n467\t        \"on\"|\"enable\")\n468\t            wifi_on\n469\t            ;;\n470\t        \"off\"|\"disable\")\n471\t            wifi_off\n472\t            ;;\n473\t \n121\t    local location_info\n122\t    location_info=$(curl -s --connect-timeout 5 \"https://ipinfo.io/$ip/json\" 2>/dev/null)\n123\t    \n124\t    if [[ -n \"$location_info\" ]]; then\n125\t  # Test with a small file download\n251\t    local test_file=\"https://httpbin.org/bytes/1024\"\n252\t    local start_time end_time duration\n253\t    \n254\t    if command_exists curl; then\n255\t =============================================================================\n283\t\n284\tnetwork_renew_dhcp() {\n285\t    local interface\n286\t    interface=$(network_get_interface_for_ip)\n287\t    \n288\t    if [[ -z \"$interface\" ]]; then\n289\t        print_error \"No active network interface found\"\n290\t        return 1\n291\t    fi\n292\t    \n293\t    print_info \"Renewing DHCP lease =============================================================================\n106\t# System Cleanup Functions\n107\t# =============================================================================\n108\t\n109\tsystem_cleanup() {\n110\t    print_header \"🧹 System Cleanup\"\n111\t    echo \"\"\n112\t    \n113\t    print_warning \"This will clean caches, logs, and temporary files\"\n114\t    if ! confirm \"Continue with system cleanup?\" \"y\"; then\n115\t        print_info \"Cleanup cancelled\"\n116\t =============================================================================\n188\t# Battery Information\n189\t# =============================================================================\n190\t\n191\tsystem_battery() {\n192\t    # Check if this is a laptop\n193\t    if ! system_profiler SPPowerDataType >/dev/null 2>&1; then\n194\t        print_info \"No battery information available (desktop Mac)\"\n195\t        return 0\n196\t    fi\n197\t    \n198\t    print_header \"🔋 Battery Information\"\n199\t    echo \"\"\n200\t    \n201\t    # Get battery info using pmset\n202\t    local battery_info\n203\t    battery_info=$(pmset -g batt 2>/dev/null)\n204\t    \n205\t    if [[ -n \"$battery_info\" ]]; then\n206\t        # Parse battery percentage and status\n207\t        local percentage status time_remaining\n208\t        percentage=$(echo \"$battery_info\" | grep -E \"InternalBattery\" | awk '{print $3}' | sed 's/;//')\n209\t        status=$(echo \"$battery_info\" | grep -E \"InternalBattery\" | awk '{print $4}' | sed 's/;//')\n210\t        time_remaining=$(echo \"$battery_info\" | grep -E \"InternalBattery\" | awk '{for(i=5;i<=NF;i++) printf \"%s \", $i; print \"\"}' | trim)\n211\t        \n212\t        echo \"  Charge: $(print_command \"$percentage\")\"\n213\t        echo \"  Status: $(print_command \"$status\")\"\n214\t        \n215\t        if [[ -n \"$time_remaining\" && \"$time_remaining\" != \"(no estimate)\" ]]; then\n216\t            echo \"  Time remaining: $(print_command \"$time_remaining\")\"\n217\t        fi\n218\t    fi\n219\t    \n220\t    # Battery health information\n221\t    local cycle_count max_capacity\n222\t    cycle_count=$(system_profiler SPPowerDataType 2>/dev/null | grep \"Cycle Count\" | awk -F': ' '{print $2}' | trim)\n223\t    max_capacity=$(system_profiler SPPowerDataType 2>/dev/null | grep \"Maximum Capacity\" | awk -F': ' '{print $2}' | trim)\n224\t    \n225\t    if [[ -n \"$cycle_count\" ]]; then\n226\t        echo \"  Cycle count: $(print_command \"$cycle_count\")\"\n227\t    fi\n228\t    \n229\t    if [[ -n \"$max_capacity\" ]]; then\n230\t        echo \"  Maximum capacity: $(print_command \"$max_capacity\")\"\n231\t        \n232\t        # Health assessment\n233\t        local capacity_num\n234\t        capacity_num=$(echo \"$max_capacity\" | sed 's/%//')\n235\t        if [[ \"$capacity_num\" -gt 80 ]]; then\n236\t            print_success \"Battery health: Good\"\n237\t        elif [[ \"$capacity_num\" -gt 60 ]]; then\n238\t            print_warning \"Battery health: Fair\"\n239\t        else\n240\t            print_warning \"Battery health: Poor (consider replacement)\"\n241\t        fi\n242\t    fi\n243\t    \n244\t    # Power adapter status\n245\t    local adapter_info\n246\t    adapter_info=$(pmset -g ac 2>/dev/null)\n247\t    if [[ \"$adapter_info\" == *\"AC Power\"* ]]; then\n248\t        echo \"  Power adapter: $(print_command \"Connected\")\"\n249\t    else\n250\t        echo \"  Power adapter: $(print_dim \"Not connected\")\"\n251\t    fi\n252\t}\n253\t\n254\t# =============================================================================\n255\t# Memory Information\n256\t# =============================================================================\n257\t\n258\tsystem_memory() {\n259\t    print_header \"💾 Memory Usage\"\n260\t    echo \"\"\n261\t    \n262\t    # Get memory statistics\n263\t    local memory_info\n264\t    memory_info=$(vm_stat)\n265\t    \n266\t    local page_size=4096\n267\t    local pages_free pages_active pages_inactive pages_wired pages_compressed\n268\t    \n269\t    pages_free=$(echo \"$memory_info\" | grep \"Pages free\" | awk '{print $3}' | sed 's/\\.//')\n270\t    pages_active=$(echo \"$memory_info\" | grep \"Pages active\" | awk '{print $3}' | sed 's/\\.//')\n271\t    pages_inactive=$(echo \"$memory_info\" | grep \"Pages inactive\" | awk '{print $3}' | sed 's/\\.//')\n272\t    pages_wired=$(echo \"$memory_info\" | grep \"Pages wired down\" | awk '{print $4}' | sed 's/\\.//')\n273\t    pages_compressed=$(echo \"$memory_info\" | grep \"Pages stored in compressor\" | awk '{print $5}' | sed 's/\\.//' 2>/dev/null || echo \"0\")\n274\t    \n275\t    # Convert to MB\n276\t    local free_mb active_mb inactive_mb wired_mb compressed_mb total_mb used_mb\n277\t    free_mb=$((pages_free * page_size / 1024 / 1024))\n278\t    active_mb=$((pages_active * page_size / 1024 / 1024))\n279\t    inactive_mb=$((pages_inactive * page_size / 1024 / 1024))\n280\t    wired_mb=$((pages_wired * page_size / 1024 / 1024))\n281\t    compressed_mb=$((pages_compressed * page_size / 1024 / 1024))\n282\t    \n283\t    used_mb=$((active_mb + inactive_mb + wired_mb))\n284\t    total_mb=$((free_mb + used_mb))\n285\t    \n286\t    echo \"  Total: $(print_command \"${total_mb} MB\")\"\n287\t    echo \"  Used: $(print_command \"${used_mb} MB\")\"\n288\t    echo \"  Free: $(print_command \"${free_mb} MB\")\"\n289\t    echo \"\"\n290\t    echo \"  Active: $(print_command \"${active_mb} MB\")\"\n291\t    echo \"  Inactive: $(print_command \"${inactive_mb} MB\")\"\n292\t    echo \"  Wired: $(print_command \"${wired_mb} MB\")\"\n293\t    \n294\t    if [[ $compressed_mb -gt 0 ]]; then\n295\t        echo \"  Compressed: $(print_command \"${compressed_mb} MB\")\"\n296\t    fi\n297\t    \n298\t    # Memory pressure\n299\t    local memory_pressure\n300\t    memory_pressure=$(memory_pressure 2>/dev/null | grep \"System-wide memory free percentage\" | awk '{print $NF}' | sed 's/%//')\n301\t    \n302\t    if [[ -n \"$memory_pressure\" ]]; then\n303\t        echo \"\"\n304\t        if [[ \"$memory_pressure\" -gt 20 ]]; then\n305\t            print_success \"Memory pressure: Low ($memory_pressure% free)\"\n306\t        elif [[ \"$memory_pressure\" -gt 10 ]]; then\n307\t            print_warning \"Memory pressure: Medium ($memory_pressure% free)\"\n308\t        else\n309\t            print_warning \"Memory pressure: High ($memory_pressure% free)\"\n310\t            print_info \"💡 Consider closing some applications\"\n311\t        fi\n312\t    fi\n313\t}\n314\t\n315\t# =============================================================================\n316\t# CPU Information\n317\t# =============================================================================\n318\t\n319\tsystem_cpu() {\n320\t    print_header \"⚡ CPU Information\"\n321\t    echo \"\"\n322\t    \n323\t    # CPU model and specs\n324\t    local cpu_name cpu_cores cpu_threads\n325\t    cpu_name=$(sysctl -n machdep.cpu.brand_string 2>/dev/null)\n326\t    cpu_cores=$(sysctl -n hw.physicalcpu 2>/dev/null)\n327\t \n333\t    echo \"  Physical cores: $(print_command \"$cpu_cores\")\"\n334\t    echo \"  Logical cores: $(print_command \"$cpu_threads\")\"\n335\t    \n336\t    # CPU usage\n337\t    echo \"\"\n338\t    echo \"  $cpu_usage\"\n344\t    \n345\t    # Load average\n346\t    local load_avg\n347\t    load_avg=$(uptime | awk -F'load averages: ' '{print $2}')\n348\t    echo \"  Load average: $(print_command \"$load_avg\")\"\n349\t}\n350\t\n351\t# =============================================================================\n352\t# Disk Usage\n353\t# =============================================================================\n354\t\n355\tsystem_disk_usage() {\n356\t    local target_dir=\"${1:-$HOME}\"\n357\t    \n358\t    if [[ ! -d \"$target_dir\" ]]; then\n359\t        print_error \"Directory not found: $target_dir\"\n360\t        return 1\n361\t    fi\n362\t    \n363\t    print_header \"💿 Disk Usage: $target_dir\"\n364\t $(print_command \"$available\")\"\n372\t        echo \"  Usage: $(print_command \"$capacity\")\"\n373\t    done\n374\t    \n375\t    echo \"\"\n376\t    print_subheader \"Largest directories in $target_dir:\"\n377\t    \n378\t    # Find largest directories\n379\t    du -sh \"$target_dir\"/* 2>/dev/null | sort -hr | head -10 | while read -r size path; do\n380\t        printf \"  %-10s %s\\n\" \"$size\" \"$(basename \"$path\")\"\n381\t    done\n382\t}\n383\t\n384\t# =============================================================================\n385\t# System Processes\n386\t# \n535\t    case \"$action\" in\n536\t        \"position\")\n537\t            dock_set_position \"$1\"\n538\t            ;;\n539\t        \"autohide\")\n540\t            dock_set_autohide \"$1\"\n541\t =============================================================================\n29\t\n30\tdev_kill_port() {\n31\t    local port=\"$1\"\n32\t    \n33\t    if [[ -z \"$port\" ]]; then\n34\t        print_error \"Port number required\"\n35\t        print_info \"Usage: mac dev kill-port <port>\"\n36\t        return 1\n37\t    fi\n38\t    \n39\t    if ! is_number \"$port\"; then\n40\t        print_error \"Invalid port number: $port\"\n41\t        return 1\n42\t    fi\n43\t    \n44\t    print_info \"Looking for processes on port $port...\"\n45\t    \n46\t    local pids\n47\t    pids=$(lsof {\n69\t    print_header \"🔗 Active Network Ports\"\n70\t    echo \"\"\n71\t    \n72\t    # Get listening ports with process information\n73\t    print_subheader \"Listening Ports:\"\n74\t    lsof -i =============================================================================\n105\t\n106\tdev_servers() {\n107\t    print_header \"🚀 Running Development Servers\"\n108\t    echo \"\"\n109\t    \n110\t    # Common development ports and their typical uses\n111\t    declare -A common_ports=(\n112\t        [3000]=\"React/Next.js\"\n113\t        [3001]=\"React (alt)\"\n114\t =============================================================================\n227\t# Process Management\n228\t# =============================================================================\n229\t\n230\tdev_processes() {\n231\t    local sort_type=\"${1:-cpu}\"\n232\t    local count=\"${2:-15}\"\n233\t    \n234\t    print_header \"🔄 System Processes\"\n235\t    echo \"\"\n236\t    \n237\t    case \"$sort_type\" in\n238\t        \"cpu\")\n239\t            print_subheader \"Top $count processes by CPU views\"\n271\t}\n272\t\n273\tdev_cpu_hogs() {\n274\t    print_header \"🔥 CPU-Intensive Processes\"\n275\t    echo \"\"\n276\t    \n277\t    ps aux | awk '$3 > 1.0' | sort -nr -k 3 | head -10 | while read -r user pid cpu mem vsz rss tt stat started time command; do\n278\t        local cmd_name\n279\t        cmd_name=$(echo \"$command\" | awk '{print $1}' | xargs basename)\n280\t        \n281\t \"$mem\" \"$pid\"\n287\t        fi\n288\t    done\n289\t    \n290\t    echo \"\"\n291\t    print_info \"💡 High CPU usage may indicate runaway processes\"\n292\t    print_info \"💡 Use 'mac dev kill-port <port>' to stop development servers\"\n293\t}\n294\t\n295\tdev_memory_hogs() {\n296\t    print_header \"💾 Memory-Intensive Processes\"\n297\t    echo \"\"\n298\t    \n299\t    ps aux | awk '$4 > 1.0' | sort -nr -k 4 | head -10 | while read -r user pid cpu mem vsz rss tt stat started time command; do\n300\t        local cmd_name\n301\t        cmd_name=$(echo \"$command\" | awk '{print =============================================================================\n318\t# Developer Utilities\n319\t# =============================================================================\n320\t\n321\tdev_json_format() {\n322\t    local file=\"$1\"\n323\t    \n324\t    if [[ -z \"$file\" ]]; then\n325\t content was not reviewed -- likely also template\"\n  ]\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n## Detailed Documentation Analysis\n\n### 1. README Quality (Score: 70/100)\n\nThe top-level README.md at 362 lines is visually well-structured and ambitious in scope. It includes badges, a quick install section, a comprehensive category table, workflow examples for three user personas (frontend developer, system administrator, development environment setup), installation options, a roadmap, and contribution guidelines. The writing quality is professional and the markdown formatting is clean.\n\nHowever, the README has significant accuracy problems that undermine its usefulness. The most severe issue is that it documents commands and features that do not exist in the codebase. The \"Configuration System\" section (lines 137-145) shows `mac config set` commands, and the \"Module Information\" section (lines 155-157) shows `mac modules list` and `mac modules info finder`. Neither of these subsystems is implemented. The main dispatcher at `bin/mac` has no route for `config` or `modules`, meaning these commands will fail with \"Unknown category\" errors. This is a significant trust violation for new users.\n\nThe architecture diagram (lines 172-189) is inaccurate in multiple ways: it lists only 6 of 9 library files under `lib/`, references `docs/commands.md` which does not exist, and uses lowercase `development.md` while the actual file is `DEVELOPMENT.md`. The file also references an Imgur-hosted screenshot image (`https://i.imgur.com/HU2yib3.jpeg`) with no local fallback, creating a fragile dependency on a third-party image host.\n\nThe README claims \"73 commands\" across 8 categories, but the actual codebase has 9 modules (the screenshot module is completely absent from the README) and the command count differs when you count dispatch cases. The `screenshot` module alone adds 11 commands that are invisible to README readers.\n\nOn the positive side, the \"Quick Commands\" section, the persona-based workflow examples, and the roadmap are well-crafted. The install instructions are clear with both automatic and manual paths.\n\n### 2. Inline Help Quality (Score: 80/100)\n\nThe inline help system is the strongest documentation asset in the project. Every module implements a `{module}_help()` function that produces visually polished output with Unicode box drawing characters, color-coded text, and consistent formatting. The help output for each module includes:\n\n- A category header with icon and module name\n- A table of commands with descriptions\n- Examples section with commented usage\n- Tips section with contextual advice\n- Global shortcuts section (where applicable)\n\nThe `mac help` main output provides a well-formatted listing of all categories with icons and descriptions. The `mac help <category>` output for each module is consistent in structure and formatting.\n\nThe search system (`mac search <term>`) is a notable feature that loads each module and queries its `_search()` function. This is consistently implemented across all 9 modules and provides useful keyword-to-command mapping.\n\nWeaknesses in the inline help: the `system` module's help does not list the `detailed-info` command even though it is implemented in the dispatch. Some help functions use slightly different column widths (65, 70, 75, 80) which creates visual inconsistency when viewing multiple modules in sequence. The finder help omits the width-matching printf format used by other modules.\n\n### 3. Developer Documentation Quality (Score: 55/100)\n\n`docs/DEVELOPMENT.md` at 593 lines is reasonably comprehensive as a contributor guide. It covers the architecture, provides a complete module template (a genuine copy-paste-ready scaffold), explains the three required functions per module, shows styling guidelines with output function examples, and provides a 5-step process for adding new modules.\n\nHowever, it has notable gaps:\n\n- **No dependencies section**: Several modules depend on optional tools (SwitchAudioSource for audio device switching, dockutil for dock app management, jq for JSON config parsing, airport for WiFi scanning). None of these are documented anywhere, including their brew install commands. A contributor running tests would not know why certain features degrade.\n\n- **No debugging workflow**: While it shows `print_debug` usage and debug mode enabling, there is no guidance on how to actually debug a module that is not loading, or how to trace command execution flow.\n\n- **Stale test instructions**: The testing section references `bash tests/test.sh [module]` but the test suite does not cover dock, audio, or screenshot modules, and the module-specific test function only handles finder, network, system, and dev.\n\n- **Missing modules from examples**: The module template examples only show 7 of 9 modules. Dock, audio, and screenshot are absent from the module list in the development guide.\n\n- **No architecture decision records**: There is no documentation explaining why certain design decisions were made (e.g., why modules are sourced rather than executed as subprocesses, why associative arrays are used for categories, why error handling uses set -euo pipefail).\n\n### 4. Code Comments Quality (Score: 65/100)\n\nCode commenting follows a consistent pattern across all modules: each file begins with a header block using `#====` separators that includes the module name, description, command listing, and CosmoLabs attribution. Functions are grouped under section headers like `# Module Functions`, `# Module Help System`, and `# Module Dispatcher`.\n\nThe comments are generally helpful but lean toward the descriptive rather than the explanatory. For instance, `finder_restart()` has comments like `# Wait for Finder to restart` before a while loop, which is useful. But the `display_set_brightness()` function has no comment explaining why the brightness value is converted from percentage to decimal (0.0-1.0), which would help future maintainers understand the AppleScript API constraint.\n\nSome header comment blocks are stale. `system.sh` header (lines 9-17) lists `login-items` and `temperature` as commands, but neither is implemented anywhere in the module. The finder header omits the `status` command. These inconsistencies between header documentation and actual dispatch functions create confusion.\n\nThe `utils.sh` file has excellent per-section documentation, with clear `#====` dividers and descriptive comments for each function group (Output Functions, Validation Functions, String Manipulation, etc.).\n\nThere is no over-commenting problem; the comment density is appropriate for a Bash project. The use of `print_debug` calls at the end of each module (`print_debug \"X module loaded successfully\"`) is a nice touch for troubleshooting.\n\n### 5. Documentation Accuracy (Score: 40/100)\n\nThis is the weakest area. The documentation has multiple categories of accuracy problems:\n\n**Commands documented but not implemented**: `mac config set`, `mac modules list`, `mac modules info` -- these appear in the README as if they work, but they will produce \"Unknown category\" errors.\n\n**Commands implemented but not documented**: The entire `screenshot` module (11 commands), the `system detailed-info` command, and the audio `up`/`down` volume commands (documented in help but not in README).\n\n**Incorrect file listings**: The README architecture tree, the install.sh download list, and the test suite module arrays all omit different subsets of the actual modules. Each list was apparently created at a different point in development and never updated when new modules were added.\n\n**Incorrect numerical claims**: The \"73 commands\" figure is repeated across multiple files (README, PROJECT_SUMMARY, PLAN) but does not match the actual count.\n\n**Stale dates and paths**: The PROJECT_SUMMARY.md contains a developer-specific absolute path. The PLAN.md references 2024 dates. The FEATURES.md is entirely a template.\n\n**Version inconsistencies**: The minimum macOS version is stated as 12.0 in README badges but 10.15 in code. The PLAN.md says Monterey+ while the code accepts Catalina+.\n\n### 6. Examples Quality (Score: 65/100)\n\nThe project provides examples in three places: the README, inline help output, and the demo system (`setup.sh demo`).\n\nThe README examples are the most comprehensive, organized by user persona (frontend developer, system admin, dev environment setup). These are well-chosen and cover realistic workflows. The \"Quick Commands\" section provides good shorthand examples.\n\nThe inline help examples in each module are practical and well-formatted, typically showing 4-5 of the most common commands with inline comments. The `dev_help()` output, for example, shows `mac dev kill-port 3000 # Kill React dev server` which provides both the command and the real-world context.\n\nThe demo system in `setup.sh` provides an interactive walkthrough that exercises the help system, safe status commands, and the search feature. This is a thoughtful addition for first-time users.\n\nHowever, there are no examples for: error scenarios (what happens when a command fails), configuration usage, the screenshot module, the audio device switching workflow, or the dock add/remove workflow with dockutil dependency. The examples also do not cover the debug mode or the `--debug` flag usage.\n\n### 7. Missing Documentation\n\nBeyond the specific findings above, several documentation categories are entirely absent:\n\n- **Error reference**: No documentation of what errors users might encounter and how to resolve them (e.g., permission errors on `network_flush_dns`, missing dependencies for audio/dock switching).\n- **Configuration guide**: The config.json file is documented nowhere. Users cannot discover that they can modify `volume_step`, `brightness_step`, or `screenshot_format` through this file.\n- **Exit codes**: No documentation of the exit code conventions (0 for success, 1 for failure).\n- **Migration guide**: No documentation for users coming from v1.x or other similar tools.\n- **Security considerations**: While DEVELOPMENT.md has a security section, there is no user-facing documentation about which commands require `sudo` and why (network_flush_dns, network_reset, system_cleanup logs all need elevated privileges).\n\n### 8. Documentation Structure\n\nThe `docs/` directory contains 26 entries including 15+ README.md files that are empty or placeholder-only in subdirectories like `planning-mode/`, `prompts/`, `workflows/`, `architecture/`, `roadmap/`, `handoffs/`, `lessons/`, `knowledge-base/`, `brainstorming/`, `feedback/`, `sops/`, `sessions/`, `release-notes/`, `instructions/`, and `bookmarks/`. This appears to be scaffolding from a project template that was never populated.\n\nThe meaningful documentation files are: `DEVELOPMENT.md` (developer guide, good quality), `PLAN.md` (project plan, somewhat stale), `PROJECT_SUMMARY.md` (duplicate of root PROJECT_SUMMARY.md), and `FEATURES.md` (unfilled template). The root-level `PROJECT_SUMMARY.md` is a 222-line celebratory document that duplicates much of the README content and adds little value.\n\nThere is significant redundancy: both `README.md` and `PROJECT_SUMMARY.md` contain the architecture diagram, command coverage table, project achievements, and example commands. `docs/PROJECT_SUMMARY.md` is an exact duplicate of the root `PROJECT_SUMMARY.md`. The `docs/PLAN.md` contains extensive project management detail that overlaps with both the README roadmap section and the PROJECT_SUMMARY milestones."}],"stop_reason":"end_turn","stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":5661,"cache_creation_input_tokens":0,"cache_read_input_tokens":91520,"output_tokens":6937,"server_tool_use":{"web_search_requests":0,"web_fetch_requests":0},"service_tier":"standard","cache_creation":{"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0},"inference_geo":"","iterations":[],"speed":"standard"}},"type":"assistant","uuid":"671b4892-2225-4b7e-bb6c-eb610b58378b","timestamp":"2026-04-07T13:19:41.211Z","userType":"external","entrypoint":"cli","cwd":"/Users/gab/PROJECTS/SuperMac","sessionId":"ee896f3b-ba3e-493e-ab51-73d0ef866e89","version":"2.1.92","gitBranch":"main","slug":"binary-sauteeing-dragonfly"}
